<span id="freeTextContainer12381181932064289476">Once upon a time came a story so full of high adventure and true love that it became an instant classic and won the hearts of millions. Now in hardcover in America for the first time since 1973, this special edition of The Princess Bride is a true keepsake for devoted fans as well as those lucky enough to discover it for the first time. What reader can forget or resist suc</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12381181932064289476">Once upon a time came a story so full of high adventure and true love that it became an instant classic and won the hearts of millions. Now in hardcover in America for the first time since 1973, this special edition of The Princess Bride is a true keepsake for devoted fans as well as those lucky enough to discover it for the first time. What reader can forget or resist such colorful characters as:<br /><br />Westley, the handsome farm boy who risks death and much, much worse for the woman he loves; Inigo, the Spanish swordsman who lives only to avenge his father's death; Fezzik, the Turk, the gentlest giant ever to have uprooted a tree with his bare hands; Vizzini, the evil Sicilian, with a mind so keen he's foiled by his own perfect logic; Prince Humperdinck, the eviler ruler of Guilder, who has an equally insatiable thirst for war and the beauteous Buttercup; Count Rugen, the evilest man of all, who thrives on the excruciating pain of others; Miracle Max, the King's ex-Miracle Man, who can raise the dead (kind of); The Dread Pirate Roberts, supreme looter and plunderer of the high seas; and, of course, Buttercup, the princess bride, the most perfect, beautiful woman in the history of the world.<br /><br />S. Morgenstern's timeless tale -- discovered and wonderfully abridged by William Goldman -- pits country against country, good against evil, love against hate. From the Cliffs of Insanity through the Fire Swamp and down into the Zoo of Death, this incredible journey and brilliant tale is peppered with strange beasties monstrous and gentle, and memorable surprises both terrible and sublime.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12381181932064289476">...more</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_14145564">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14145564" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/858949-chris" class="left imgcol" title="Chris"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1208350750p2/858949.jpg" alt="Chris" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/14145564?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 25, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/858949-chris" class="user" title="Chris">Chris</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=top-shelf" class="actionLinkLite">top-shelf</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14145564">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9403460089011362147">If you haven't read this book, then all I can tell you is to go out, get it, and read it. Now. Don't bother with the rest of this review, you'll thank me later. It has:<br /><br />Fencing.<br />Fighting.<br />Torture.<br />Poison.<br />True Love.<br />Hate.<br />Revenge.<br />Giants.<br />Hunters.<br />Good men.<br />Bad men.<br />Beautifulest ladies.<br />Snakes.<br />Spiders.<br />Beasts of all natures and descriptions.<br />Pain.<br />Death.<br />Brave men.<br />Coward men.<br />Strongest men.<br />Chases.<br />Escapes.<br />Lies.<br />Truths.<br />Passion. <br />Miracles. <br /><br />For a start.<br /><br />It's one of the greatest love/action/revenge stories ever abridged</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9403460089011362147">If you haven't read this book, then all I can tell you is to go out, get it, and read it. Now. Don't bother with the rest of this review, you'll thank me later. It has:<br /><br />Fencing.<br />Fighting.<br />Torture.<br />Poison.<br />True Love.<br />Hate.<br />Revenge.<br />Giants.<br />Hunters.<br />Good men.<br />Bad men.<br />Beautifulest ladies.<br />Snakes.<br />Spiders.<br />Beasts of all natures and descriptions.<br />Pain.<br />Death.<br />Brave men.<br />Coward men.<br />Strongest men.<br />Chases.<br />Escapes.<br />Lies.<br />Truths.<br />Passion. <br />Miracles. <br /><br />For a start.<br /><br />It's one of the greatest love/action/revenge stories ever abridged by a modern author. Well, it seems that Mr. Goldman felt that the <em>original</em> story, as written by the immortal S. Morganstern, was a little too dry for public consumption, as well as damaging to treasured childhood memories, so he went through it and put together this "good parts" version, and the world is a better place for it. [1:]<br /><br />Of course, the big gag is that there never was an original version of the book. There never was an S. Morganstern, the greatest of the Florinese writers. Goldman's father may have read books to him as a child, but he never read <em>this</em> book to him. The entire thing is a fiction, beginning to end, but Goldman sells it really well. He tells the tale of how he blossomed as a boy - going from being a sports-obsessed disappointment to a ravenous bookworm, all thanks to this book. He talks about trying to give the same gift to his son, who manages to make it through one chapter before giving up in exhaustion. He talks about the great shock of discovering that his father had done something utterly brilliant - he had skipped the dull bits and left the exciting parts intact.<br /><br />Knowing that all of this is false certainly doesn't detract from the story. It's a story about a story, and the effect that a story can have on a young mind. Or any mind, for that matter. It's about how stories can teach us lessons that only later we understand - such as how life is not fair - and how stories can change us in ways that we never expected. It's about our relationship with fiction, and with the world around us. In his fictional childhood, Goldman learned more about the world from the process of watching the story unfold than he did from the story itself. And so this book is a story about stories. The <em>actual</em> story is just bonus.<br /><br />Which brings me, of course, to the film. Let me say that this is one of the very, very few instances where I will put the movie up on par with the book. 99.9999 repeating percent of the time, the book is better than the movie. This is one instance where they are equal in nearly every measure. I'm sure a lot of this has to do with the fact that Goldman wrote the screenplay for the film, so not only is the story intact, but a great deal of the dialogue is almost verbatim from the book. It was gold in print and gold on the screen. The hardest part about reading the book is trying not to hear Andre the Giant, Christopher Guest, Robin Wright and all the other fine actors and actresses in your head as you read.<br /><br />So, whether you read the book or see the movie, you're in for a treat. And as you read, just remember the books that molded you into who you are today. Think about the stories that taught you life's lessons before life got around to doing it. Think about them and appreciate them, and remember that every book is a lesson, one way or another....<br /><br />[1:] This is a fun type of meta-fiction, writers writing autobiographically about writing about books that never existed. I find it interesting that <em>The Princess Bride</em> can sit comfortably shoulder-to-shoulder with <em>House of Leaves</em>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9403460089011362147">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_164264025">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164264025" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1805180-seak" class="left imgcol" title="seak"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" alt="seak" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/164264025?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 07, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1805180-seak" class="user" title="seak">seak</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780345418265" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2012" class="actionLinkLite">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer164264025">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2190697726985950546">First of all, anyone who's rated this less than 5 stars is just wrong, very wrong. I know this because I was recently instated "Master of all Opinions" where mine is the most rightest. :)<br /><br /><strong>The Structure</strong><br /><br />I guess the real place to start with this book is with its structure. You may have noticed that the actual title is - The Princess Bride: S. Morgenstern's Classic Tale of True Love and High Adventure: The "Good Parts" Version Abridged by William Goldman.<br /><br />Whew. That's a mouthful.<br /><br />But that's also the ge</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2190697726985950546">First of all, anyone who's rated this less than 5 stars is just wrong, very wrong. I know this because I was recently instated "Master of all Opinions" where mine is the most rightest. :)<br /><br /><strong>The Structure</strong><br /><br />I guess the real place to start with this book is with its structure. You may have noticed that the actual title is - The Princess Bride: S. Morgenstern's Classic Tale of True Love and High Adventure: The "Good Parts" Version Abridged by William Goldman.<br /><br />Whew. That's a mouthful.<br /><br />But that's also the genius of this book. You see, S. Morgenstern's "Classic" doesn't actually exist, only this abridged, "Good Parts" version, created wholly by William Goldman. This may not be the first time I expound upon the genius of this narrative.<br /><br />The Princess Bride begins much like the movie. William Goldman gets sick and his father comes in to read him this story. Only in the book, we don't jump right into the story, we go to the future of Goldman's life where he talks about things that actually happened in his life, but also some thing's he's made up.<br /><br />For instance, Goldman talks about writing for <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0064115/">Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid</a>, which he did do. But he also talks about his fictional psychotherapist wife (that took some research). <br /><br />Finally, about 40 or so pages in, we get to the actual story. And it's almost exactly like the movie, or at least I should say that nothing is left out of the book that's in the movie (except the performances, but I'll get there). And that's how it should be, Goldman did write the screenplay.<br /><br />During this time, Goldman explains that the book is actually extremely boring in parts and while he was young, his father only read the "good parts." Instead he skipped the pages and pages of explanations of Florintine (the actual story taking place in the fictional Florin) ancestry, which is also explained as Morgenstern being satiric. <br /><br />The story begins and just like in the movie, there are multiple interruptions, but in the book they're made as editorial notes. Again, this is where the genius of this setup comes in. He's able to comment on his own story, add things that the story alone cannot do, even point out things he finds odd...in his own story.<br /><br />An example of Goldman pointing out what he finds odd is that throughout the story (not the editorial notes), there are always interruptions in the form of parentheticals. For instance:<br /><br />"...she examined herself pore by pore in her mirror. (This was after mirrors.)"<br /><br />"'I'll leave the lad an acre in my will,' Buttercup's father was fond of saying. (They had acres then.)"<br /><br />"Then, rather than continue the argument (they had arguments then too), they would both turn on their daughter."<br /><br />These were found throughout the book and always made me laugh, but Goldman has an editorial note explaining that if the parentheticals bother you, you should skip them. <br /><br /><strong>The "Good Parts" and The Movie</strong><br /><br />If you're like me, you've seen the movie so many times that you can quote just about everything, and I'm terrible at quoting movies. <br /><br />The movie itself follows the book excellently and even exceeds the book in many ways. It's so very rare, but the already excellent characters such as Fezzik and the Man in Black are almost across the board improved upon in the movie.<br /><br />I mean, how do you get any better than Andre the Giant and Billy Crystal's performance of Miracle Max. I was reading the exact same words that Crystal says, but it was almost flat in the book, whereas in the film, Crystal makes them come alive.<br /><br />But the benefit of the book is, as usual, the fact that you get inside the character's heads and backstory. Before each of the famous "fight" scenes between The Man in Black and Buttercup's three kidnappers, we are let in on the backstory of each. These are great. <br /><br />We see what actually happened with <strong>
  <u>Inigo</u>
</strong> and why he seeks revenge and becomes the greatest swordsman in the world...well, almost. We find out that <strong>
  <u>Fezzik</u>
</strong> is even big for a Turk (who average 15 pound babies) and how he was a competitive fighter who had to learn how to lose to make the crowd like him. And best of all, it goes into his obsession with RHYMING! Then there's <strong>
  <u>Vizzini</u>
</strong>, the self-proclaimed genius and orchestrator of this most unstoppable team of the world's best.<br /><br />This is another thing I loved about this book. Goldman's obsessed with numbers. Buttercup starts out as not even in the top 20 of the most beautiful women in the world, but quickly jumps to the top. Prince Humperdink is the best hunter in the world. Buttercup and Westley's kiss is better than the top 5 kisses ever had.<br /><br />This just adds to the epic and fairytale feeling of the story, it can't get more noble than the best of the best, but at the same time, the whole numbering thing is just another comical aspect of Goldman's writing. The fact that people would even have a list or the ability to measure such things. I love it.<br /><br />Do I need more examples of the genius of this work? The wit, the charm, the characters that are larger than life, this is easily one of my favorite books of all time.<br /><br /><u>5 out of 5 Stars</u> (This wasn't even a debate)<br /><br /><strong>Buttercup's Baby</strong><br /><br />This is a short story and addition to the 30th anniversary edition of the book. I'm never a fan of these sorts of things. To be honest, it just messes with the purity that is the original and can leave you with a sour taste in your mouth. The Matrix (the movie) should have been left alone along with things like Ender's Game and Dune. It really is okay to leave people with a sense of wonder and imagination at what could have happened instead of milking things for all they're worth.<br /><br />With that said, this wasn't a terrible addition, it was just unnecessary. It deals with the time after the ending of The Princess Bride when everyone lives "happily ever after." The first chapter is "Fezzik Dies," so already you're world is shattered. <br /><br />Buttercup's baby is stolen and Fezzik is chasing the culprit, but then it never really goes back to this, it goes to a couple chapters that only slightly fit together (even admitted by Goldman), but which explains how they get to someone running away with Buttercup's baby.<br /><br />Before this story is an explanation of how this story came about (in the fictional way, not an actual explanation) and it involves how Stephen King was actually going to do the abridgement, but left it up to Goldman. I guess I just don't get these parts.<br /><br />I'm sure this is better for people who have read the story ages ago and come back to something new, but reading them all together just messed with the original too much.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2190697726985950546">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12499446299102635116">I love this book and the movie. <div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_718830515">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/718830515" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may" class="left imgcol" title="Emily May"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1402215455p2/4622890.jpg" alt="Emily May" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/718830515?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 20, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may" class="user" title="Emily May">Emily May</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/438353.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780156035217" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014" class="actionLinkLite">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer718830515">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4002019729704229670">It's amazing that I've never found time to read this book before. I have seen the movie, but it was years ago and I only really remember the one thing that everyone remembers:<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400545604i/9686920.gif" /><br /><br />The real strength of this book is that is just ticks every box imaginable. It's a fairy tale, full of action, romance and revenge, and it has that timeless quality that the best fairy tales seem to carry. It was published in the 1970s but it feels like it should be a thousand years old, passed down from generation to genera</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4002019729704229670">It's amazing that I've never found time to read this book before. I have seen the movie, but it was years ago and I only really remember the one thing that everyone remembers:<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400545604i/9686920.gif" /><br /><br />The real strength of this book is that is just ticks every box imaginable. It's a fairy tale, full of action, romance and revenge, and it has that timeless quality that the best fairy tales seem to carry. It was published in the 1970s but it feels like it should be a thousand years old, passed down from generation to generation. It's non-stop adventure, comedy gold and full of some of the most memorable characters I've ever had the pleasure of reading about.<br /><br />Goldman's writing style for this novel works so surprisingly well. For one, it's such an unusual idea to write a retelling of a story by a fictional author - Goldman claims his father read him the S. Morgenstern classic as a child and then proceeds to tell us the "abridged" version with all the good parts. It's strange how well his constant sidenotes actually add to the story, rather than take us out of it. <strong>I think maybe it's the little kids inside most readers who remember the magic of being read a story as a child.</strong> Because while this is a fantasy story with magic and princesses, it's also a bittersweet tale about how a father introduced his son to the world of stories.<br /><br />And I found it hilarious. I want you to know how rare it is for me to find a book that successfully combines silly humour with dramatic action and adventure. I've struggled with authors like Terry Pratchett because I felt the humour took away any serious investment I may have had in the story. But this book quietly mocks itself on every page and it works so well. At first I wondered if I would be rolling my eyes at the whole notion of Buttercup as "the most beautiful woman in the world", but Goldman rolls his eyes for us with the comic portrayal of obsession with beauty and true love. <br /><br /><strong>The characters here are so rich and vivid that it's hard to imagine that they don't exist somewhere in an alternate fantasy world.</strong> Everyone remembers and loves Inigo Montoya and the pretty-faced Westley, but I was surprised by Buttercup. My memory of the movie seems to have done her a disservice because I remembered her as a typical, beautiful princess. But no, Buttercup is fierce and brave. She might be silly and naive at the start but she grows and develops with age. She doesn't sit back and let things happen to her, which I like.<br /><br /><strong>Honestly, this was a delight to read. I can't believe I waited so long.</strong><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk">Blog</a> | <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.leafmarks.com/emilymay">Leafmarks</a> | <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews">Facebook</a> | <a rel="nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01">Twitter</a> | <a rel="nofollow" href="http://instagram.com/emleemay">Instagram</a> | <a rel="nofollow" href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4002019729704229670">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_37807428">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37807428" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1413439-stephen" class="left imgcol" title="Stephen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" alt="Stephen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/37807428?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 05, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1413439-stephen" class="user" title="Stephen">Stephen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780345418265" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=humor-and-satire" class="actionLinkLite">humor-and-satire</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=swashbucklers" class="actionLinkLite">swashbucklers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=1970-1979" class="actionLinkLite">1970-1979</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer37807428">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6043206206743010781">5.0 stars. HOW AMAZINGLY GOOD IS THIS BOOK YOU ASK?....so good it is almost<br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Decorated%20images/?action=view&amp;current=kijinnmaru-inconceivable.jpg"> <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380318894i/689646.jpg" /></a><br /><br />This is a literary treasure and one that I can not recommend more highly. Let me start by saying that prior to reading this book I had probably seen the movie version a dozen times or so and ABSOLUTELY LOVE IT!! I only mention this so that you know where I'm coming from in case you are not a fan of the movie as I think if you like one you will like the other and, conversely, if you didn’t like the movie, the book may not</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6043206206743010781">5.0 stars. HOW AMAZINGLY GOOD IS THIS BOOK YOU ASK?....so good it is almost<br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Decorated%20images/?action=view&amp;current=kijinnmaru-inconceivable.jpg">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380318894i/689646.jpg" /></a><br /><br />This is a literary treasure and one that I can not recommend more highly. Let me start by saying that prior to reading this book I had probably seen the movie version a dozen times or so and ABSOLUTELY LOVE IT!! I only mention this so that you know where I'm coming from in case you are not a fan of the movie as I think if you like one you will like the other and, conversely, if you didn’t like the movie, the book may not appeal to you as much. <br /><br />As for the book, I was AMAZED at what a superb adaptation of the novel the movie was. Along with the Lord of the Rings trilogy and No Country for Old Men, this may be the best adaptation of a classic novel that I have ever come across. This may lead you to ask whether it is even worth it to read the book given that much of what is in the book is on the screen. My answer to that would be a resounding YES!! <a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Awesomeness/?action=view&amp;current=Win.jpg">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380318894i/689647.jpg" /></a><br /><br />First of all, the book is as much fun as the movie and the tone of the writing is unique, playful and very funny. Despite knowing the plot of the book intimately, I found the reading experience to be fresh and new. <br /><br />I am going to assume that people reading this have seen the movie, read the book or at least have an understanding of the basic plot. If not, the book description and other reviews do a very good job of explaining it. Instead, I thought it might be helpful to mention those parts of the book that were not included in the movie or that I thought the book’s treatment was superior (i.e. Book is Better) and those aspects of the movie that I thought were superior to the source material (i.e. Movie is Better). <br /><br /><strong>BOOK IS BETTER</strong>:<br /><br />1.	Prince Humperdinck’s Zoo of Death (not mentioned in the movie and I thought it was interesting and gave great insight into the character).<br /><br />2.	The Book does a much better job than the movie in describing Prince Humperdinck as a truly evil person and thus a top notch villain. <br /><br />3.	The book contains a whole Chapter on Inigo Montoya that provides details of his childhood and his Father’s original encounter with the Six Fingered Man (this is dealt with in a very brief conversation in the movie). I really enjoyed the expanded version.<br /><br />4.	The book also contains a whole chapter on Fezzik and shows his childhood and early years. This was excellent and I really liked learning about his trouble in adapting to deal with his enormous size. <br /><br />5.	The beginning of the book describes how Buttercup becomes the “most beautiful woman in the world” and the fate of the women in front of her. This is absolutely HYSTERICAL. I wish they would have found a way to incorporate this into the movie because it was very enjoyable. <br /><br />6.	All of the interruptions in the Narrative where the author is explaining why he cut out whole sections of the original Morgenstern novel (the fictional novel of which this novel was supposedly the abridged “good parts”) were very funny and made the book a unique experience. <br /><br /><strong>MOVIE IS BETTER</strong>:<br /><br />1.	I must begin with Miracle Max. The book is really good, but Billy Crystal was absolutely AMAZING (as was Carol Kane who played Miracle Max's wife). Crystal’s dialogue in the movie was better than the book and is a great example of making the original even better without messing with the feel of the story. <br /><br />2.	Wallace Shawn as Vizzini (pictured above) gives a truly great comic performance and made the Movie version of the character even more fun then the book version. All I kept hearing in my head whenever he was on stage in the book was him shouting INCONCEIVABLE!!<br /><br />3.	Similarly, Mandy Patinkin as Inigo Montoya is another example of amazing casting that made the on screen version of the character even more fun than the book version. <br /><br />4.	The final scene between Westley and Prince Humperdinck was more fun in the movie than in the book. <br /><br />Bottom-line, if you have enjoyed the movie but have not read the book, I strongly recommend it. Similarly, if you have read the book and have not seen the movie, I strongly recommend that as well. Both are terrific.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6043206206743010781">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer3470857">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer534753285419753988">I am one of the few people in the world who does not think the book is better than the movie here. There is an undercurrent of bitterness in this book that I find off-putting. I am given to understand by a friend that those elements--i.e., the autobiographical stuff in Goldman's own persona--are actually fictional. But I found that they soured my enjoyment of the story they framed. I couldn't enjoy the writing of a writer who seemed as misanthropic and hateful as Goldman came off to me. TPB is s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText534753285419753988">I am one of the few people in the world who does not think the book is better than the movie here. There is an undercurrent of bitterness in this book that I find off-putting. I am given to understand by a friend that those elements--i.e., the autobiographical stuff in Goldman's own persona--are actually fictional. But I found that they soured my enjoyment of the story they framed. I couldn't enjoy the writing of a writer who seemed as misanthropic and hateful as Goldman came off to me. TPB is still a great book--better than three stars, but I couldn't quite bring myself to give it four.<br /><br />Stick to the movie. It has the opposite problem, but you can always fast forward through the saccharine Fred Savage bits.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200054545" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer" class="left imgcol" title="Anzu The Great Destroyer"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1381756864p2/2278800.jpg" alt="Anzu The Great Destroyer" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/200054545?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 28, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer" class="user" title="Anzu The Great Destroyer">Anzu The Great Destroyer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6283231-the-princess-bride" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">hopeless romantics</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=the-hate-it-burns" class="actionLinkLite">the-hate-it-burns</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=lots-of-kisses-and-mushy-stuff" class="actionLinkLite">lots-of-kisses-and-mushy-stuff</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=el-clasico" class="actionLinkLite">el-clasico</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=fat-kitty-judges-you" class="actionLinkLite">fat-kitty-judges-you</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=fantasy-something" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-something</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=is-it-just-me-goddammit" class="actionLinkLite">is-it-just-me-goddammit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=whiny-bitches" class="actionLinkLite">whiny-bitches</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=d-oh" class="actionLinkLite">d-oh</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=dat-cover-goddammit" class="actionLinkLite">dat-cover-goddammit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=masters-of-snoozeville" class="actionLinkLite">masters-of-snoozeville</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=lust-at-first-sight" class="actionLinkLite">lust-at-first-sight</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=cheesetacular" class="actionLinkLite">cheesetacular</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=good-guy-greg" class="actionLinkLite">good-guy-greg</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=i-am-disappoint" class="actionLinkLite">i-am-disappoint</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=well-arent-you-mister-popularity" class="actionLinkLite">well-arent-you-mister-popularity</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=facepalm" class="actionLinkLite">facepalm</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=not-my-cup" class="actionLinkLite">not-my-cup</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=reviewed-2013" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed-2013</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer200054545">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3796679292648836243">I’m sorry Kate’s favorite book, but I must destroy you. <br /><br />Two stars. Yep, I am one of those people. Cynical. Have no heart. Have no good taste in books. Just want mindless action and independent sword-wielding women as main characters. Don’t like overpowered men. Nor women, for that matter. Don’t believe in love at first sight. Hate damsels in distress. Hate perfection. You get the point.<br /><br />Do you see why I didn’t like the book? Do you? Well, if you’ve read it you probably do. If you didn’t, then go</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3796679292648836243">I’m sorry Kate’s favorite book, but I must destroy you. <br /><br />Two stars. Yep, I am one of those people. Cynical. Have no heart. Have no good taste in books. Just want mindless action and independent sword-wielding women as main characters. Don’t like overpowered men. Nor women, for that matter. Don’t believe in love at first sight. Hate damsels in distress. Hate perfection. You get the point.<br /><br />Do you see why I didn’t like the book? Do you? Well, if you’ve read it you probably do. If you didn’t, then go ahead and read it. <br /><br />I dare you to read it.<br /><br /><em>The Princess Bride</em> started out as an entertaining read. Bill Goldman’s part in the story was a pleasant surprise, even though he didn’t seem like the kindest person out there, I found myself immersed in the story. When the so called “introduction” ended and the actual <em>Princess Bride</em> story began... well, my enthusiasm started to decrease. The more I read the more it decreased.<br /><br />“What were you expecting from a book called “<em>The Princess Bride</em>”?” my husband asked. Well, I thought it may be a parody of all those cheesy romance books that are way too popular than they deserve. Maybe I thought it was a new take on those romances, something that would make me say “Gee, this is one good romance novel. I sure feel silly for bashing the genre so much in my reviews.” I wanted more or less the same true-love-conquers-all story but with better characters. Yes, the characters are the ones who made me dislike the book. <br /><br />My main problem is Buttercup. Oh god how can I express the amount of hatred I feel for this girl? A gif? Would it be appropriate? Sure, why not?<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357224ra/708565.gif" /><br /><br />She was such a fucking idiot! I can’t believe it. I feel sad to know that the great super-ninja assassin Westley fell for her because she’s so hawt. Don’t worry, I hate Westley just as well, but the thought of everyone wanting to get Buttercup only because she’s incredibly beautiful makes me very angry. Yes, I know things were like that back then. Yes, I know this is not a new idea. Too many books have this “fairest of them all” crap. But that doesn’t change the fact that it makes me angry. Foam at the mouth. Rage. Want to tear things into pieces and then burn them. Yes, burn everything.<br /><strong>
  <em>
    <blockquote>Buttercup was what he thought of. Her autumn hair, her perfect skin, and he brought her very close beside him, and had her whisper in his ear throughout the burning: "I love you. I love you. I only left you in the Fire Swamp to test your love for me. Is it as great as mine for you? Can two such loves exist on one planet at one time? Is there that much room, beloved Westley? . .</blockquote>
  </em>
</strong><br />Barf.<br /><br />I can swallow this “fairest of them all” shit <strong>if</strong> the character has a purpose other than making beautiful, and hopefully male, babies.<br /><br />Well.. Buttercup didn’t. Surprised? No, you shouldn’t be.<br /><blockquote> <strong><em> "Woman," Westley roared, "you are the property of the Dread Pirate Roberts and you . . . do . . . what . . . you're . . . told!" </em></strong> (Westley is the Dread Pirate Roberts so… yeah. There you go.) </blockquote><br />Westley… well my main problem with the dude is that he is overpowered. Sure, the ending made up for it, he did end up being a zombie and all that (ick, try kissing him now Buttercup) so he is not as perfect as one would think. Nice try, Goldman. Nice try.<br /><br />No. The dude is still too overpowered. He is a wannabe ninja who can master any art on his own and can train his mind into standing the most intense of pain. Take that sensei! No one can be better than the all-awesome Westley! NO ONE!!<br /><strong>
  <em>
    <blockquote> “Which pain will be least endurable? The physical, or the mental anguish of having freedom offered if the truth is told, then telling it and being thought a liar." <br />"I think the physical," said the Prince. <br />"I think you're wrong," said the Count. <br />Actually, they were both wrong; Westley suffered not at all throughout. His screaming was totally a performance to please them; he had been practicing his defenses for a month now, and he was more than ready. </blockquote>
  </em>
</strong><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380357224i/708566.jpg" /><br /><br />Dude. Two words. Get real.<br /><br />I think the reason why I couldn’t enjoy this is the fact that I’m old and bitter. Ok, not as old as you would think, I’m merely 25 atm, but I think I would have enjoyed this more at an earlier age. <em>The Princess Bride</em> needs a decent amount of innocence in order to strike home.<br /><br />On the other hand, I wouldn’t let any children near it. It’s slightly too violent and full of fucked up people. But that’s just me.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3796679292648836243">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_7089424">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7089424" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/437515-echo" class="left imgcol" title="Echo"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1191618892p2/437515.jpg" alt="Echo" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/7089424?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 09, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/437515-echo" class="user" title="Echo">Echo</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780345418265" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/437515-echo?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/437515-echo?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/437515-echo?shelf=books-in-14" class="actionLinkLite">books-in-14</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7089424">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15331578224566669885">I feel the need to gush. I've set aside the many books I want to read for the moment in favor of rereading this one. I loved it when I read it way back in about the sixth grade, so I thought it was time I give it another shot.<br /><br />As much as I loved it as a kid, I love it more now. Maybe because I can appreciate it on different levels. I'm only about halfway through on my reread, but I've come to the conclusion that Goldman is a genius. The story, characters, and dialogue are impressive enough, but t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15331578224566669885">I feel the need to gush. I've set aside the many books I want to read for the moment in favor of rereading this one. I loved it when I read it way back in about the sixth grade, so I thought it was time I give it another shot.<br /><br />As much as I loved it as a kid, I love it more now. Maybe because I can appreciate it on different levels. I'm only about halfway through on my reread, but I've come to the conclusion that Goldman is a genius. The story, characters, and dialogue are impressive enough, but then you add in the whole bit about Morgernstern. I mean, here Goldman wrote this amazing story, and then he makes up a story about another man who wrote the story. Then he makes up a fictional story about his father reading him this story written by someone else, and later about his process of "abridging" the story. He even makes up a fictional wife and son who play their own parts in this. He throws in asides written by himself, and asides written by Mogernstern, and asides written by himself about the asides written by Morgernstern. He claims to have written a reunion scene that readers can request to have sent to them by the publisher, and when people did write in for it, Goldman sent them back a letter all about the legal reasons he could not send them the scene - all fictional, of course. (The man had me going for years. I read this thing when I was in sixth grade, mind you. I didn't realize there was no S. Morgernstern until I was in college.)<br /><br />Anyway, while I was absolutely enthralled with this book, it occured to me today that I would put it on par with some of the greats, like Twain. The literary devices, the story, the wit, the satire (I think he's even satiric regarding satire itself) - I don't care if it got turned into a silly movie with a cult following*, I think this one of the few modern books I've read that I'd call Literature.<br /><br />Plus, you know, it's also an amazing story. Zoo of Death, the most beautiful woman in the world, the Dread Pirate Roberts, a prince plotting murder to start a war, a hunchback criminal mastermind, a giant, the greatest swordfighter on the planet, true love, revenge . . . who doesn't love that sort of thing? The man is a genius.<br /><br /><br />* No disrespect of the movie intended. It's good. Mind you, it was the first movie I'd watched that I'd read the book first, and it devastated me. I mean it absolutely broke my heart. None of the charactes looked right. Everything was changed. The sharks were turned into eels. This person spoke a line meant for that person. Things were left out. It was all wrong. It just wasn't the book and I didn't like it. I've resigned myself to it since then, and admitted that yes, the movie is good and I forgive it it's shortcomings. It did the best it could. The movie can't help it it's not as amazing as the book. There are so many things that just can't be translated to film, and there's no help for it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15331578224566669885">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_22060568">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22060568" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/164338-mack" class="left imgcol" title="MacK"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1183463108p2/164338.jpg" alt="MacK" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/22060568?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 25, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/164338-mack" class="user" title="MacK">MacK</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780345418265" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/164338-mack?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/164338-mack?shelf=contemporary" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/164338-mack?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer22060568">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16094407580302328810">I'm a little biased when it comes to this book. Yes, I saw the movie first and it made me happier than anything I've ever seen before or since. Yes, I do consider how much a person likes <em>The Princess Bride</em> before determining how good a friend to be with them. (I don't insist on it, but it can queer a good friendship)<br /><br />I'm not alone in this, but I do share a similar affinity for the book, despite discrepancies that may make others blanche. And even for me Fezzik will always be a Frenchman and not a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16094407580302328810">I'm a little biased when it comes to this book. Yes, I saw the movie first and it made me happier than anything I've ever seen before or since. Yes, I do consider how much a person likes <em>The Princess Bride</em> before determining how good a friend to be with them. (I don't insist on it, but it can queer a good friendship)<br /><br />I'm not alone in this, but I do share a similar affinity for the book, despite discrepancies that may make others blanche. And even for me Fezzik will always be a Frenchman and not a Turk, and Goldman's "Zoo of Death" will be forever confused with "The Pits of Despair" but these are minor points.<br /><br />The fact is that Goldman is a hell of a writer. The movie is great because it uses his screenplay wonderfully. The book is fantastic becasue he employs all his talents. He is a master of dialogue (what else would you expect from a man with two screenplay Oscars?), he details setting and character with a few quick flashes of his pen, and he has enough acerbic wit to have created what is, at once, both a brilliant satire of fairy tales and a compellingly readable fairy tale in its own right.<br /><br />One of the surprising things is that Goldman sticks so doggedly to the conceit that there is an S. Mogenstern, a country called Florin, and that the novel is at once really "abridged" rather than written by him, and that everything actually does happen.<br /><br />That becomes a trifle irritating, you almost want the man to admit that: "yes, I am the man, I did write something that is beloved and adored and will be passed down from generation to generation, just as I claimed this book was passed down to me. Only, it is all me. My imagination, my genius, bow down and praise me!"<br /><br />But he doesn't. And that, though irritating, is actually one of the best things about the book. Goldman himself suspends his disbelief and forces us to do the same. Imagination takes hold at the beginning and our immersion in it makes every page, every quip tantalizing to behold and easy to savor.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16094407580302328810">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_24683465">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24683465" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/768443-veronica" class="left imgcol" title="veronica"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1207727134p2/768443.jpg" alt="veronica" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/24683465?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 05, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/768443-veronica" class="user" title="veronica">veronica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780345418265" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">10 year olds</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/768443-veronica?shelf=childhood-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">childhood-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer24683465'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer24683465">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11831263166835351669">I know there are people who LOOOOOOOVE the film, "The Princess Bride." While I thoroughly enjoy the movie, I think I may only LOOVE it. I mean, Inigo Montoya is FABULOUS and I really really dug Westley, and the pwiest was vewwy vewwy funny!!!! So, when someone was kind enough to lend me the book, I had relatively high expectations. Now, don't get me wrong, I wasn't <em>disappointed</em> in <em>The Princess Bride</em>, but I just wasn't thrilled or moved to laugh till I cry (which the movie sometimes can).<br /><br />First of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11831263166835351669">I know there are people who LOOOOOOOVE the film, "The Princess Bride." While I thoroughly enjoy the movie, I think I may only LOOVE it. I mean, Inigo Montoya is FABULOUS and I really really dug Westley, and the pwiest was vewwy vewwy funny!!!! So, when someone was kind enough to lend me the book, I had relatively high expectations. Now, don't get me wrong, I wasn't <em>disappointed</em> in <em>The Princess Bride</em>, but I just wasn't thrilled or moved to laugh till I cry (which the movie sometimes can).<br /><br />First of all, let's get all English-major on this, and talk about the meta-layered frame narratives going on in this novel. Holy cow! First of all, keep in mind that the book's title is <em>The Princess Bride, S. Morgenstern's Classic Tale of True Love and High Adventure</em>. Basically, what Goldman does is this -- he tells his readers that the book they are holding in their hand (his book) is actually the abridgment of the original PB written by this invented author, Morgenstern. As a child, says Goldman (within the novel, not in the introduction or anything), his father read PB to him aloud, and the boy fell in love with the book. When, as a father himself, he attempted to pass on this beloved childhood novel to his very fat and very spoiled son, he is shocked to find out that the boy can't get into the book -- because it is too long and too boring! It turns out that Goldman's father, when reading to the boy, had skipped hundreds of pages of political and historical satire! So, when Goldman's own son attempted to read the book, he found it overly dry and long. This leads Goldman to undertake the task of abridging PB and basically re-publish the book as his father had read it to him -- just the adventure plot and the romance.<br /><br />While bearing this in mind, you must remember that Goldman is making all of this up. There is no Morgenstern, no original PB. The project in itself is quite interesting and it had me excited at reading a book that really messed with the reader's perception of narrator, of what's real and what isn't. Goldman often includes long parenthesis in which he bitches about his frigid wife or his snotty son, or over some of the stunted romantic liaisons that he failed at. All in all, I must say, that the actual narrator of PB comes off as an ego maniacal and pathetic loser who happens to have been the screenwriter for some awesome movies (think "Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid," "Misery." (One interesting aside is the confrontation between Goldman and Stephen King over supposedly abridging the sequel to PB, called <em>Buttercup's Baby</em>, a conversation in which they discuss Kathy Bates' performance in "Misery.")<br /><br />Once you get over the self-loathing and self-loving that the narrator is indulging in while writing this book, you get to the actual storyline. Westley hearts Buttercup, but she is to be married to Prince Humperdink. Meanwhile, Inigo Montoya searches for his father's six-fingered murderer, Fezzik plods along like a dumb giant, and about 300 pages into the novel, these 2 team up with Westley in an attempt to steal Buttercup away from Humperdink.<br /><br />The good news is that some of the movie's best scenes are taken verbatim from the book. Inigo Montoya is as fabulous here as he is in the movie. Actually, even more so, because you get a pretty in depth history of his childhood, his training, his thought process. He is by far the most interesting character in the novel.<br /><br />The scene with Miracle Max is also as rewarding as it is in the movie, and the funniest scene in the book is the marriage (mawwiage) scene.<br /><br />Still, a couple interesting scenes do not a great novel make, and for once, I may have found a book that I enjoyed less than its film adaptation! Ring the bells and sound the alarms!!<br /><br />Ah, and I see God is agreeing with me! I have just looked out of our great scenic window, and the most BEAUTIFUL rainbow has just appeared.<br /><br />To wrap up, I must say that I was left a bit deflated by <em>The Princess Bride</em>. It has a little zing, a little sappy romance, and a little adventure, but overall, I think I approached it about 15 years too late. Had I read it when I was 10, I'm sure it would still to this day be one of my favorites.<br /><br />P.S. Take one "Hello. My name is Inigo Montoya. You killed my father. Prepare to die." Repeat until it becomes unnerving. Result -- the best scene in the novel and the film, by a landslide. Oh, Inigo. I love you. And in this book, only you. I should pull a Goldman and abridge <em>The Princess Bride</em> and leave in only Inigo's part, and add on to his story line. Food for thought! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11831263166835351669">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_46393915">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46393915" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1572236-robin" class="left imgcol" title="Robin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1237804938p2/1572236.jpg" alt="Robin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/46393915?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 15, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1572236-robin" class="user" title="Robin">Robin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780345418265" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Robin by: </span>
      GoodReads Fantasy Book Club
  </div>



    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer46393915">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8538448712711937967">What a charming read. This is one of the few books where I saw the movie first then read the book. I think William Goldman's book was largely "unknown" until the movie came out.<br /><br />Like Shawshank Redepmtion and Stand by Me (Based on the novella The Body) this is one of the most accurate book to screen apdaptations. It is almost verbatium from the book and the few variations (Zoo of Death rather than Pit of Despair) have no real impact on the story.<br /><br />Being as I edit fantasy (visa-vie my husband's books</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8538448712711937967">What a charming read. This is one of the few books where I saw the movie first then read the book. I think William Goldman's book was largely "unknown" until the movie came out.<br /><br />Like Shawshank Redepmtion and Stand by Me (Based on the novella The Body) this is one of the most accurate book to screen apdaptations. It is almost verbatium from the book and the few variations (Zoo of Death rather than Pit of Despair) have no real impact on the story.<br /><br />Being as I edit fantasy (visa-vie my husband's books) I do often look for and find "plot holes" and there is a big one in this story. When Inago hears the torment cry of Westley he assumes it this the man in black because he was enganged to Buttercup but of course he had no reason to suspect anything between the two of them them. Even so I see this as just a kind of "cool thing I saw" it did not diminish the book for me in anyway.<br /><br />Now for the big difference between the book and the movie. The book is littered with "asides" from William Goldman where he discusses parts in the original Simon Morgenstern version that he omitted to "keep only the good parts". He presents his book as an "abridgement" of Morgenstern's original and both praises and condems Morgensterns original work. He goes on to give tidbits such as a "reunion scene" that he wrote but could not include because his editor felt it was wrong for someone abridging someones elses work to add anything.<br /><br />If you have any of the "aniversary editions" (I read the 30th) there are other bonus materials such as recounts of the numerous law suits between the Morgenstern Estate and Goldman and a dispute where they were trying to get Stephen King to write the Sequel "Buttercup's Baby" instead of Goldman. <br /><br />Goldman even gives us glimpses into his personal life talking about both his failed marriage and his son (and how much he had to go thorugh to get him a copy of Morgenstern's Princess Bride for his 10th bithday).<br /><br />I'm sorry to say that I fell for Goldman's farce hook, line and sinker. It was only after I tried to find Morgenstern's original work that I discovered that everything in The Princess Bride is fiction including all the asides. That made me appreciate the work even more. The lengths to which Goldman went - (even inventing a familiy and various other characters, editors, lawyers, agents, etc was great. I particularly liked that he told people to write into the publisher to receive a copy of the "missing reunion scene" only to take the farce further by sending them letters that he could not comply due to pending litigation!<br /><br />The one and only disappointment in this "farce in the bonus material" is the horror which is "Buttercup's Baby". This is presented as yet another abridgement of Morgenstern;'s work but only the first chapter as the estate debates whether he or King will "get the job". BTW I'm sure King is "in" on this whole farse and loves it as Goldman and King have worked on several projects together such as Misery. The story is terrible and certainly comes no where near the brillance of The Princess Bride. I can see why Goldman never wrote the sequel and to be honest I hope he never does. The Princess Bride was so sublime and perfect we should be left with this and nothing more.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8538448712711937967">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_654332417">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/654332417" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3807932-megan" class="left imgcol" title="Megan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1408910509p2/3807932.jpg" alt="Megan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/654332417?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 16, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3807932-megan" class="user" title="Megan">Megan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/438353.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780156035217" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3807932-megan?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3807932-megan?shelf=2013" class="actionLinkLite">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer654332417">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9658364334783941486">After reading The Princess Bride I realized that this was the book I needed to use to end my review drought. This book has everything you could ever possibly want in a book. There is romance, adventure, comedy, princess and princes, pirates, giants, sword fights, poison, and rodents of unusual size. Is there anything that this book is missing? It is inconceivable how good this book really is. <br /><br />I saw the movie for the first time when I was little. My parents had mentioned it before but I never gav</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9658364334783941486">After reading The Princess Bride I realized that this was the book I needed to use to end my review drought. This book has everything you could ever possibly want in a book. There is romance, adventure, comedy, princess and princes, pirates, giants, sword fights, poison, and rodents of unusual size. Is there anything that this book is missing? It is inconceivable how good this book really is. <br /><br />I saw the movie for the first time when I was little. My parents had mentioned it before but I never gave it any thought, thinking it was probably just a crappy old movie. I've never been so wrong in my life. When I finally watched it, it became an instant favorite of mine. Like William Goldman, this was a story that I loved when I was sick. Like I said it had everything and the name Humperdinck always made me giggle for some reason. Alright it still makes me giggle. The movie has been a part of my life ever since. Even when I got to college it became my roommates favorite movie as well. Whenever it was just me and her home alone we would instantly put on the Princess Bride. When our other roommates would get home they would just groan and say, "You guys are watching this movie again?" Yeah we watched it that much. It is sad that our conversations sometimes are exclusively quotes from the movie, and the sadder part is the conversations make sense. So why if I loved the movie so much has it taken me 21 years to finally read the book? The honest answer is that I have no idea. I had picked up the book in the bookstore so many times that if I had a penny for every time I touched it I probably could have bought it a few times or got a really nice hardcover edition. <br /><br />Having been a lover of the movie for so long I can honestly say the book was as good, if not better, than the movie. In a way having seen the movie before reading the book made it better in a way. For example Wallace Shawn screaming INCONCEIVABLE in my head, or Mandy Patinkin delivering Inigo's famous line, and Billy Crystal as Miracle Max. Having those voices and characters in my head brought the humor in the book to another level. <br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427256r/854106._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />The whole structure of the book is interesting in itself. William Goldman writes the book as if it is an abridged novel, the original being by S. Morgenstern. He cuts out all the boring parts leaving only the "good parts" just like when his father read it to him when he was little. Throughout the novel we get interrupted by Goldman describing why he took out certain parts and giving himself more backstory. While sometimes these parts were entertaining, other times they were not. I'm not sure if this was just part of the person he was betraying himself as or if it was how he actually was, but he seemed very full of himself at times, especially during the introductions and the explanation of Buttercup's Baby. I didn't really care about his conversation with Stephen King about Kathy Bates, I just wanted to read the story not about how awful his wife and son were. But again some of those parts I found witty, just not very many of them. And I especially don't like how he kept teasing about a reunion scene that doesn't exist. <br /><br />There were parts in the book that I wish were in the movie. My favorite parts were the backstories of Fezzik and Inigo. In the movie we know the Count killed Inigo's father and you were pulling for him, but his backstory just made you root for him harder. Even though I knew the outcome I still found myself cheering for Inigo to win and being heartbroken when he gets a dagger thrown in his side and you think for a second that he is going to lose. With Fezzik we didn't really know any of his backstory from the movie. In the book we learn of how his mother and father made him fight even though he never really wanted to. He is just one of those giants that looks threatening but in reality is a big teddy bear. In the book I found myself many times wanting to reach through the pages and give Fezzik a big hug, well comparatively it would be a little hug. Fezzik and Inigo were by far my favorite characters of the novel. I like how Goldman introduces the characters. At first they are merely known as the giant and the Spaniard that kidnapped Princess Buttercup and you are rooting against them. But then you learn their names and their backstories and all of a sudden you are cheering for them. Then you have the lovers Westly and Buttercup.They possess true love, I'm sorry twu luv, which keeps them fighting for each other throughout the novel. While often times it was meant to be over the top the love scenes never came off as cheesy and gag-worthy, though the young William Goldman thought they were. But then again I'm a girl and often times like that romantic stuff. <br /><br />The greatest part of this book is all the wonderful one-liners. I could quote this book/movie all day long. "Hello, my name is Inigo Montoya, you killed my father, prepare to die!" Or my mom's favorite, "Inconceivable!" "You keep using that word, I don't think it means what you think it means." She makes me rewind the movie if she misses that line. My personal favorite line was smaller in the book but still made me laugh, "Mawidge." My roommate has told me many times that when I give a speech at her wedding it better be that cause apparently I'm fairly good at sounding like the priest! <br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427256r/854107._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Included after the Princess Bridge Goldman included the first chapter of Buttercup's Baby. Yeah just the first chapter, thanks Goldman. I really enjoyed learning what happened to Westly, Buttercup, Inigo, and Fezzik after the end of The Princess Bride. The chapter starts out running (literally) and before you know it, it was over. I kept flipping back and forth as if by some magic more of the story would appear. I'm a bit peeved that Goldman would did this. I wanted, no I need, more of the story. Sorry to spoil it for people but the chapter is called "Fezzik Dies," and that's where he leaves you. He leaves you hanging with all these questions and then is all like "I'm sorry they won't let me abridge the rest of the novel." Thanks Goldman. <br /><br />But besides that I absolutely loved this book. It is definitely one of my favorites. If you have seen and liked the movie you need to read the book. If you haven't seen the movie you need to go and rent it right now, you have been missing out or go and read the book, you just need to experience The Princess Bride. <strong>6/5 stars</strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9658364334783941486">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
