<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_46420320">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46420320" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/811687-sandi" class="left imgcol" title="Sandi"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1404709147p2/811687.jpg" alt="Sandi" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/46420320?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 18, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/811687-sandi" class="user" title="Sandi">Sandi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/438353.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780156035217" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=2009" class="actionLinkLite">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer46420320">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16391754643753616105">I'm probably spoiled because I have seen the movie version of "The Princess Bride" about a gazillion times. As I read, I just pictured Robin Wright, Cary Elwes, Mandy Patikin, et al. as the characters. I even heard their voices in the dialog. That said, "The Princess Bride" is a brilliantly executed concept. It's really a novel within a novel as Goldman tells a fiction story about his relationship with S. Morgenstern's "The Princess Bride" and his path to abridging it so it only has the "good pa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16391754643753616105">I'm probably spoiled because I have seen the movie version of "The Princess Bride" about a gazillion times. As I read, I just pictured Robin Wright, Cary Elwes, Mandy Patikin, et al. as the characters. I even heard their voices in the dialog. That said, "The Princess Bride" is a brilliantly executed concept. It's really a novel within a novel as Goldman tells a fiction story about his relationship with S. Morgenstern's "The Princess Bride" and his path to abridging it so it only has the "good parts". I must admit to reading my own "good parts" version as I skipped the numerous introductions, including the fictional introduction to the fictional chapter from the fictional sequel, "Buttercup's Baby". I found Goldman's asides about the writing and publication process to be quite amusing. <br /><br />If possible, I would give "The Princess Bride" 3-1/2 stars. The basic story is wonderfully funny and romantic and exciting. But, the pages and pages of introduction and prologue and some of the asides detract from the main story. The movie keeps this stuff to a minimum, having only a few scenes of Peter Falk reading the book to Fred Savage. In this case, I believe the movie is superior to the book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16391754643753616105">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer117033914">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4478652809025103050"><strong>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/23160533-shandra">Shandra</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12045894-annette-booknerderie">Annette</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5028851-cathryn">Cathyrn</a> May 24</strong><br /><br />Actual Rating 4.5 stars<br /><br /><blockquote> <em>There is no room in my body for anything but you. My arms love you, my ears adore you, my knees shake with blind affection. My mind begs you to ask for something so it can obey. Do you want me to follow you for the rest of your days? I will do that. Do you want me to crawl? I will crawl. I will be quite for you or sing for you, if you are hungry, let me bring you food, or if you have thirst and nothing will quench it but Ara</em></blockquote></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4478652809025103050"><strong>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/23160533-shandra">Shandra</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12045894-annette-booknerderie">Annette</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5028851-cathryn">Cathyrn</a> May 24</strong><br /><br />Actual Rating 4.5 stars<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>There is no room in my body for anything but you. My arms love you, my ears adore you, my knees shake with blind affection. My mind begs you to ask for something so it can obey. Do you want me to follow you for the rest of your days? I will do that. Do you want me to crawl? I will crawl. I will be quite for you or sing for you, if you are hungry, let me bring you food, or if you have thirst and nothing will quench it but Arabian wine, I will go to Araby, even though it is across the world, and bring a bottle back for your lunch. Anything there is that I can do for you, I will do for you; anything there is that I cannot do, I will learn to do. Dearest Westley, darling Westley, adored Westley, sweet perfect Westley, whisper that I have a chance to win your love.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />*le sigh*<br /><br />Epic stories are my favorite. Maybe its the world building, the swords and sorcery, the kings and queens, wizards and medicine men. That is something that sparks my interest, but when you add in a epic love story I'm all in. <br /><br />Now, this book is almost word for word the same as the movie. There are some things left out, like Fezzik and Inigo looking for Westley going through the different levels of the zoo. Prince Humperdinck and Count Rugen were darker and slimmier than I expected. Buttercup was much more annoying, not in a bad way. And Westley was perfect! I think really enjoying these characters in raw form made this book so much better than the movie. <br /><br /><strong>Fezzik</strong><br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401589355ra/9821910.gif" /><br /><br /><em>"Stupid, stupid, go and wait for Vizzini with Cupid"? That rhymed, but where was the Cupid? <br /><br />"Dummy, dummy, go out now and fill your tummy." That rhymed too, but what kind of instructions were those?<br /><br />What to do, what to do?<br /><br />"Dunce, dunce, use your brains and do it right for once."?</em>
</blockquote> <br /><br /><br /><br /><strong>Inigo Montoya</strong><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401589543ra/9821928.gif" /><br /><br /><em>"I, Inigo Montoya, do challenge you, coward, pig, killer, ass, fool, to battle."<br /><br />"Enough of your family is dead for one day; be content," said the noble.<br /><br />"When you beg me for your breath, then I shall be contented. Now <strong>dismount!"</strong><br /><br />The nobleman dismounted. <br /><br />"Draw your sword."<br /><br />The nobleman unsheathed his killing weapon. <br /><br />"I dedicate your death to my father," Inigo said. "Begin."</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><strong>Westley</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401589543ra/9821929.gif" /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>As you wish.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><strong>Buttercup</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388255956ra/7779683.gif" /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>The boys.<br />The village boys.<br />The beef-witted featherbrained rattleskulled clodpated dim-domed noodle-noggined sapheaded lunk-knobbed boys.<br /><br />How could anybody accuse her of stealing them? What good were they? All they did was pster and vex and annoy. <br /><br />"Can I brush your horse, Buttercup?"<br />"Thank you, but the farm boy does that."<br />"Can I go riding with you, Buttercup?"<br />"Thank you, but I really do enjoy myself alone."<br />"You think you're too good for anybody, don't you, Buttercup?"<br />"No; no I don't. I just like riding by myself, that's all."</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />*On a side note: I love her in the House of Cards.*<br /><br /><br />I think I can leave out Prince Humperdinck and Count Rugen cause they are slimy and I do not like them! They were actually better characters in the book than in the movie. <br /><br />I'm glad I finally got to read this book.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1048793957">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14292641711511365243">I absolutely loved <a title="The Silent Gondoliers by William Goldman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21776.The_Silent_Gondoliers">The Silent Gondoliers</a>. It was just a perfect gem in every way, 5 stars was not enough reward for it's brilliance. With that in mind I was hyped to read The Princess Bride and not ready at all for the experience.<br /><br />When I lived in Jerusalem I used to leave the snowy heights in winter for the perpetual summer of the Dead Sea, the lowest place on earth, about an hour away. Swimming was impossible, the water buoyed you up, rejected you even so that body parts were impossible to keep</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14292641711511365243">I absolutely loved <a title="The Silent Gondoliers by William Goldman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21776.The_Silent_Gondoliers">The Silent Gondoliers</a>. It was just a perfect gem in every way, 5 stars was not enough reward for it's brilliance. With that in mind I was hyped to read The Princess Bride and not ready at all for the experience.<br /><br />When I lived in Jerusalem I used to leave the snowy heights in winter for the perpetual summer of the Dead Sea, the lowest place on earth, about an hour away. Swimming was impossible, the water buoyed you up, rejected you even so that body parts were impossible to keep submerged. It was such fun, an amazing experience, something really special. After that I would run for the deep pools of fresh spring water to wash the salt off my skin. You jump in and sink to the bottom. It is a shock to the brain after the floating on the Dead Sea. You can't prepare yourself for the sinking, it is like an optical illusion, but a sensory one instead. And so it was with the Princess Bride.<br /><br />For me, it just sank like a stone beneath the consciousness of the fun and perfection of the Silent Gondoliers. There you go. Maybe I will watch the film one day, I hear it is better.</span>

              <a href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-astute-crabbist?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-astute-crabbist?shelf=young-adult-books" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-astute-crabbist?shelf=all-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">all-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer82974581">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1654782367461954328">This book has its moments, but I'm not sure what all the fuss is about. It's all very clever and playful and a little bit silly. But for all the originality in the telling, it really doesn't end up anywhere worth going. I did enjoy it on the whole, but I found my mind straying quite a bit thanks to a lot of "device" and not enough story. Said device being the premise that the story is an abridgment of a very old classic, with the "abridger" insinuating himself into the story to tell you about th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1654782367461954328">This book has its moments, but I'm not sure what all the fuss is about. It's all very clever and playful and a little bit silly. But for all the originality in the telling, it really doesn't end up anywhere worth going. I did enjoy it on the whole, but I found my mind straying quite a bit thanks to a lot of "device" and not enough story. Said device being the premise that the story is an abridgment of a very old classic, with the "abridger" insinuating himself into the story to tell you about the parts he cut out. <br /><br />I'm surprised at the very high average rating for the book. My guess would be people loved the movie so much that they let this high opinion inflate their ratings of the book. The film is much more entertaining than the book. Goldman's work in the film industry is strongly evident in the book, and many of the joke scenes are better viewed than read. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1654782367461954328">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9962038998095055501">I can't believe I thought Morgenstern was real. Not for long, really. But still.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText9962038998095055501">I can't believe I thought Morgenstern was real. Not for long, really. But still. When I discovered he wasn't I hated this book for a while.<br />But then I reread it and it was awesome in an entirely new way. I'm still not a huge fan of the fake little tidbits that the "abridgment" offers, especially the allusions to Florin as a real place, but I generally just skip over those. Also, I find the story of Goldman and his fat kid vaguely depressing. And I didn't like the part about Westley wearing jeans. That's just silly. But everything else was excellent.<br /><br />I wonder if he's ever actually going to write Buttercup's Baby. I don't like the idea of the giant-talking-bird-thing that he mentions in the thirtieth-anniversary-edition...Maybe just because I don't like birds. They're creepy. Extra creepy if they're giant and they speak.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_206392201">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206392201" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3333119-vanessa" class="left imgcol" title="Vanessa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1422139828p2/3333119.jpg" alt="Vanessa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/206392201?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 30, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3333119-vanessa" class="user" title="Vanessa">Vanessa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2794395-the-princess-bride" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3333119-vanessa?shelf=faves" class="actionLinkLite">faves</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3333119-vanessa?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3333119-vanessa?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer206392201">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1648346214245134644">I am currently writing this review, having stayed up all night with the beginnings of a cold, and being sick from something I ate yesterday.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I live on my own and both my male grandparents are no longer with us, so I didn't get to sit up in bed and listen to S. Morgenstern's classic tale of true love and high adventure – the 'good parts' version – being narrated by my grandfather, like the kid in the movie. Also, my dad is generally too busy, so that cuts William Goldman's own accou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1648346214245134644">I am currently writing this review, having stayed up all night with the beginnings of a cold, and being sick from something I ate yesterday.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I live on my own and both my male grandparents are no longer with us, so I didn't get to sit up in bed and listen to S. Morgenstern's classic tale of true love and high adventure – the 'good parts' version – being narrated by my grandfather, like the kid in the movie. Also, my dad is generally too busy, so that cuts William Goldman's own account out of the picture.<br /><br />No, my friends. I had to read this all by myself, whilst sat in bed nursing a nasty case of the rumbly tumbly and the drippy nose. But what the hey, I bet that's how most of us read it. Unless, of course, we happen to be of Florinese or Guilder lineage?<br /><br />Okay, enough about the movie, more about the book. This book is so damn <em>happy</em>. It clearly loves the fairytale tropes it pokes fun at, and there's never any sour feeling to the satire. As Mel Brooks once said, you've got to love the genre you're parodying. <em>The Princess Bride</em> has its tongue firmly placed in its cheek, and the humour it employs is absolutely delicious. <br /><br />I know the story basically inside out, because my brother used to make me watch the movie all the time when we were growing up. (We shared a room with bunk-beds for five years. Ain't that cute.) Of course, I do really like the movie, and reading the book is a nice little compliment. It follows the film pretty much <em>exactly</em>. Honestly, it's the most faithful book to movie adaptation you will ever see. ...Well, excepting Goldman's occasional commentary on the story, which was turned into the grandfather reading to his grandson in the movie.<br /><br />Goldman's commentary is hilarious. He satirises university professors who read way too much into what is a pretty simple story, how so many classics have a ridiculous amount of unnecessary information crammed into their pages (like the wardrobes and hat collections of the queen and the countess, if I remember correctly)... you get the idea. And it's true – we do skim to the 'best parts' of fairy tales, and perhaps sanitise them a little bit for the young audience. I have a pretty vivid memory of my mum reading me <em>The Little Mermaid</em>, and hastily adding 'and they lived happily ever after', which seemed a little suspect. I looked in the book some time later, and indeed, we had the edition in which the poor little mermaid dies by turning into sea foam.<br /><br />Speaking of this, though, both ways work wonderfully as a storytelling device. William Goldman's writing is a cross between a traditional fairy tale and a work of comedic genius. In fact, it mostly reminds me of the Discworld books, except with perhaps a little bit more knowing winks at the reader every now and again. That's a pretty good thing to be, in my book.<br /><br />The dialogue is also hilarious. I mean, come on. You have a master swordsman whose response to seeing his father murdered by a nobleman is to train around the continent for ten years and rehearse the famous line: 'My name is Inigo Montoya. You killed my father. Prepare to die.' And then when he does catch up to his father's murderer, the Count runs away squealing like a coward. In my head, the look on Inigo's face at that moment is absolutely priceless.<br /><br />Also, for a traditional fairy tale, it ends in a pretty silly way, but it fits the story absolutely perfectly. I also love how it's open to interpretation, enflaming the imaginations of children everywhere. Didn't anyone else ever imagine alternate endings to their favourite fairy tales? Clearly, seeing as there have been <em>so many</em> <strong>DAAARK</strong> fairy tale retellings in the cinemas recently. (Keep your greasy mitts off this one, though, Hollywood.)<br /><br />I adored this book and I'm really glad I read it after tracking down a copy on back-order. My cover is a little bit dorky – a sentiment felt by me and the lady at the book shop, but what the hey. I'm going to give this a 5/5. It's short, sweet, and an absolutely wonderful read.<br /><br />(Also, as I learned when I finished this book, William Goldman wrote <em>Marathon Man</em>, which has 'made him famous in dentists' offices all around the globe.' Pfft.)<br /><br />(This review is also available on my blog: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://book-wyrm.blogspot.co.uk/2013/01/book-review-princess-bride-by-william.html" target="_blank">http://book-wyrm.blogspot.co.uk/2013/...</a>)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1648346214245134644">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12812658019677782905">GOLDMAN, you GENIUS. You had me going there. :D Seriously, I wanted to write to his publishing company to read his version of the reunion scene.<br /><br />Initial Thoughts:<br />1. "Wait a minute... I thought this was... Okay, maybe it isn't. WAIT. IS IT REALLY? Hmmm..." I was asking myself this while I was reading this book so many times! When I finished the book, and finally had to confirm or bust my questions, I was laughing. That's how awesome Goldman's writing is. :D And that's what I loved most about this</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12812658019677782905">GOLDMAN, you GENIUS. You had me going there. :D Seriously, I wanted to write to his publishing company to read his version of the reunion scene.<br /><br />Initial Thoughts:<br />1. "Wait a minute... I thought this was... Okay, maybe it isn't. WAIT. IS IT REALLY? Hmmm..." I was asking myself this while I was reading this book so many times! When I finished the book, and finally had to confirm or bust my questions, I was laughing. That's how awesome Goldman's writing is. :D And that's what I loved most about this book, the reading experience.<br />2. LOVE all the characters. Inigo is my favourite, but I love the man in black, Buttercup, and Fezzik as well. Really great drama and intensity with all of the characters. I also enjoyed the back stories, especially Inigo's.<br />3. Funny! The humour is actually subtle. With the combination of dramatic scenes, and thorough narrative, the humour balances everything out, making for a fun and fast read.<br />4. So many great elements. From fencing, to revenge, torture, love, and magic, you have more than enough to stimulate your imagination.<br />5. Seriously. I wanted to get a copy of S. Morgenstern's book. X)<br /><br />Love the movie adaptation as well! The tone between the two are completely different, and the film doesn't include back stories, but the dynamic between all the actors and humour is AMAZING!<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=v04ojoYfDtw">Check out my book and movie video review here!</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/758091000?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 28, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/25353295-carmen" class="user" title="Carmen">Carmen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published" class="actionLinkLite">traditionally-published</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer758091000">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17639092804572725840">One of the best books ever written.<br /><br />ETA: Re-read 01/28/2015<br />Wow, I haven't read this book in about five years and I forgot a lot of things about it. For one thing, this time I read the 30th anniversary edition. For another thing, I read it cover to cover instead of skipping over Goldman's "this is my life" crap. I don't like reading his thoughts.<br /><br />I'm not as enamored of this book as I was when I was younger (I used to have the whole first chapter (The Bride) memorized). Things strike me now that did</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17639092804572725840">One of the best books ever written.<br /><br />ETA: Re-read 01/28/2015<br />Wow, I haven't read this book in about five years and I forgot a lot of things about it. For one thing, this time I read the 30th anniversary edition. For another thing, I read it cover to cover instead of skipping over Goldman's "this is my life" crap. I don't like reading his thoughts.<br /><br />I'm not as enamored of this book as I was when I was younger (I used to have the whole first chapter (The Bride) memorized). Things strike me now that didn't in, let us say, more innocent years. :) For one thing, Westley slaps Buttercup's face, and I just can't brook that kind of behavior. As my good friend always says, "There's scum, and then there's men who hit women." Yeah. Especially with all the "true love" stuff thrown in.<br /><br />So, we've established that Westley is the kind of <s>man</s> scum who lays hands on a woman, and we've got problems with Buttercup herself - she's like a beautiful brainless Barbie. And she's stupid and selfish and basically useless in any kind of crisis, I was so angry with her for leaving Westley to the wolves (metaphorically) when they get out of the Fire Swamp. But at least she suffered greatly for it in the days leading up to her marriage to Humperdinck. It seems like Westley got off scot-free.<br /><br />Such a big deal is made out of Buttercup's beauty that it makes me uncomfortable. If she was plainer, would Westley have fallen in love with her? There's not much to her besides being gorgeous. She's not even particularly kind or noble and she has no skills. It makes me upset in books when it is obvious a person is "in love" with another person solely on the basis of their physical appearance. I wish I could say there was more to Buttercup and Westley than this, but there really isn't. And she only loves Westley because he's good-looking and obedient.<br /><br />Lastly, it's a satire. I should lighten up, right? LOL Well, as you've noticed, this is a five-star book for me. Even though it's lost something since I first read it at age 13, it's always been a beloved book of mine and I own a yellowed, battered, well-loved copy. It's always going to have a special place in my heart.<br /><br />ETA: 02/08/2015 Sorry, I can't keep this on my "favorites" shelf or keep the five-star rating. It's not the book I thought it was 10 years ago.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17639092804572725840">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_955442029">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/955442029" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans" class="left imgcol" title="?? Sarah ?? (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442730799p2/7298986.jpg" alt="?? Sarah ?? (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/955442029?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans" class="user" title="?? Sarah ?? (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)">?? Sarah ?? (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/9525672-the-princess-bride" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=kindle" class="actionLinkLite">kindle</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=read-2014" class="actionLinkLite">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer955442029">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer943820768121116824"><strong>Dnf at 60%.</strong><br /><br />How do you even begin to review a much-loved classic when you didn’t even manage to finish it? I tried. I really tried to like this book. But no, it just wouldn’t happen. To think this is Kate Daniels’ favourite book! To think the Beast Lord himself tells her “as you wish” at the end of Magic Burns! Why oh why couldn’t I like this book?! Oh well, I guess it can’t be helped.<br /><br />So, let’s start from the beginning. I had a problem with this particular edition from the very first pages. First</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText943820768121116824"><strong>Dnf at 60%.</strong><br /><br />How do you even begin to review a much-loved classic when you didn’t even manage to finish it? I tried. I really tried to like this book. But no, it just wouldn’t happen. To think this is Kate Daniels’ favourite book! To think the Beast Lord himself tells her “as you wish” at the end of Magic Burns! Why oh why couldn’t I like this book?! Oh well, I guess it can’t be helped.<br /><br />So, let’s start from the beginning. I had a problem with this particular edition from the very first pages. First we have the introduction to the 30th edition: I read it and thought “wow that was tedious, this Goldman is pretty full of himself isn’t he?” Okay, so here I am ready to enjoy the story. But no, not happening. First you have to read the introduction to the 25th edition. Seriously? The first introduction wasn’t annoying enough so the publishers decided to add a second one? Oookay… I know I should have skipped it but I didn’t: more presumptuous blabbering courtesy of Goldman. Who does this guy think he is anyway?! I must admit, I wasn’t in the best disposition when I started reading the actual story, which probably didn’t help. Soooo, I finally get to the story, yay! Except not. Before you read the story you have to suffer through Goldman’s explanation as to why he supposedly decided to retell Morgenstern's tale. I understand this is part of the story too and it’s not completely uninteresting but at this point I just wanted to read to the freaking Princess Bride! No more Goldman talking about Goldman! <br /><br />And so the story begins! Surprising as it may sound, I loved it at first. Well, I loved the first chapter. Then it all went downhill pretty fast, or, as we French put it, it collapsed like a soufflé. To put it plainly: I was bored to death (I said that already didn’t I?) and I didn’t like the characters at all. Buttercup: beautiful (yes I got that the first time you wrote it, no need to re-hash every two seconds) and utterly useless. I like my heroines badass and butt-kicking (too much UF I’m afraid) so Buttercup and I were on a collision course from the start. Westley: is this guy for real? Doesn’t he have a single flaw? I mean, how perfect can you get? Boring, boring, boring. Come to think of it, what bothered me most here is that the whole thing was so completely, absolutely cliché from beginning to end (which is quite ironic when you think of it, since the story is supposed to be a parody of the genre). I guess I should have thought twice about reading the book because it is, after all, a fairytale. Strangely enough, I was expecting a fairytale with a twist, something that would make it less… fairytale-y I guess. Don’t know why. I did see the movie when it first came out and enjoyed it (as far as I can remember). Then again, I was only a teenager at the time and the whole damsel in distress thing might have appealed to me then. <br /><br />So there you have it. I didn’t like it. I don’t even know why I’m giving it two stars since I didn’t even finish it. Oh well, I might not be a fairytale kind of girl but I too have a heart. Make of it what you will. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="943820768121116824">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/270582502?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 22, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7585217-lynn" class="user" title="Lynn">Lynn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer270582502">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12346188645973336363">Continuing my "loved the movie so let's try the book" escapades, I am shocked to write that this book is every bit as awesome as the movie. It's, it's (wait for it) INCONCEIVABLE!! I love the movie and was initially concerned that the book would be a let down. But then I saw a whole host of rave reviews and figured it would be safe to dive in. It was not only safe, but as much fun as I could possibly have hoped for. It's just, just (here it comes again) INCONCEIVABLE how good this is. <br /><br />Now there</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12346188645973336363">Continuing my "loved the movie so let's try the book" escapades, I am shocked to write that this book is every bit as awesome as the movie. It's, it's (wait for it) INCONCEIVABLE!! I love the movie and was initially concerned that the book would be a let down. But then I saw a whole host of rave reviews and figured it would be safe to dive in. It was not only safe, but as much fun as I could possibly have hoped for. It's just, just (here it comes again) INCONCEIVABLE how good this is. <br /><br />Now there are parts of the movie that I think were better, Miracle Max played by Billy Crystal being the first to spring to mind, but there are also quite a few areas where the book is superior, the intro and the portrayal of the Prince as a real villain are examples. My advice is to see the movie and read the book. And then do both again over and over as they both just keep getting better. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12346188645973336363">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_58596889">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/58596889" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/841949-tracey" class="left imgcol" title="Tracey"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1325394892p2/841949.jpg" alt="Tracey" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/58596889?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 15, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/841949-tracey" class="user" title="Tracey">Tracey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7313640-the-princess-bride" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=old-favorite" class="actionLinkLite">old-favorite</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=pirates" class="actionLinkLite">pirates</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=5-star" class="actionLinkLite">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer58596889">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7261428959729005550">I hereby solemnly swear (my word as a Spaniard) not to commit the cliché of using the "I" word in this review, in any context.<br /><br />And once again: it's been ages since I read this. So very long. So – many thanks to the <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/46745">#GeekGirls Book Club</a> (<a rel="nofollow" href="http://geekgirlsbookclub.blogspot.com/">also here</a>)for making this the December book – it might have been another age before I got around to it again. <br /><br />I remember the sheer and utter delight of reading something that hadn't been butchered in the film version – which has, of course, much to do with the fac</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7261428959729005550">I hereby solemnly swear (my word as a Spaniard) not to commit the cliché of using the "I" word in this review, in any context.<br /><br />And once again: it's been ages since I read this. So very long. So – many thanks to the <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/46745">#GeekGirls Book Club</a> (<a rel="nofollow" href="http://geekgirlsbookclub.blogspot.com/">also here</a>)for making this the December book – it might have been another age before I got around to it again. <br /><br />I remember the sheer and utter delight of reading something that hadn't been butchered in the film version – which has, of course, much to do with the fact that William Goldman wrote the screenplay. I'm sure it's been said before that if this book is the "Good Parts Version" of S. Morgenstern's Classic Tale of True Love and High Adventure (which, in case there's somehow, bizarrely, any question, is fictional) (there's no such person as S. Morgenstern) (just saying), the movie is the "Good Parts Version" of this book. The book is lovely – but my first love was the movie. (Reading the pertinent section: <em>What do you mean sharks? They were shrieking eels! I'm telling you, you're messing up the story! Now get it right! </em>) I'm ashamed to say that it took some time for the book to grab hold of me this time. But once I was hooked I was well and truly hooked, and loved every minute.<br /><br />I remember seeing it in the theatre: it was one of those movies whose commercials hit every right button and exerted a strong dragging force toward the nearest cinema. But my sister and I dithered or were busy or what-have-you, and finally went to see it a couple of weeks into the run. It was only playing in Southington, and Southington, for me at least, is a terrible, terrible place, by which I mean I've never been there but I got very, very lost. Not merely lost – where-the-hell-am-I hours-and-hours lost. And, yes, that night we got lost. A little. It wasn't me driving, so it was just a little. And we were a bit late – not hours and hours, since I wasn't driving – and when we went into the theatre the previews were over and it was pitch dark. We stopped dead just inside the doors, and one of us said she hoped we didn't sit on anyone, and we gingerly made our way on in and sat down. And when the screen cast some more light on the audience we laughed, because we would have had to have tried to sit on someone: there were two other people in the place.<br /><br />It was an instant addiction, and we both quoted it inaccurately for months until the VHS came out (or we could see it on HBO, whichever came first), and then we quoted it incessantly and more correctly. I was thrilled when I discovered the book, and devoured it immediately. But I think I've only read the book the once, whereas I watch the movie fairly regularly. <br /><br />And then when I started wandering about online I came to find that <em>The Princess Bride</em> is the gold standard of geekdom. Whatever else you're a fan of, if you're a geek you know TPB. Whatever your accomplishments or abilities (or lack thereof), if you can answer "Stop it now! I mean it!" appropriately, you're acceptable. If you can do the whole "Bye bye boys!" scene, you're good. If you can do the whole iocaine powder sequence verbatim, or perhaps Miracle Max's scene in its entirety, then you have indeed reached a pinnacle. <br /><br />Sadly, I think my problem with the book is that there is no "Stop it now! I mean it!" moment, as such. Fezzik rhymes, yes, but not then and there – and that is symptomatic of why it took me weeks to make my way through the first third of The Good Parts Version. The whole scene surrounding "I don't think it means what you think it means", for example, is much wordier and less streamlined than the movie scene; that happens several times, and it's a revelation to see how much is done with a look or one line in the film that takes a paragraph in the book. That was what took so long to get used to, Goldman's chatty, Oy Vey style; at times it was a little like Miracle Max telling the whole story – only not quite as whiplash funny. Still funny, very ("The Sicilian Crowd (two was company, three a crowd, even then)"), but paced very differently. For example, the simple line "Unemployed? In Greenland?" was far more succinct and simple (and funny) than the explanation in the book. The upshot: the book is outstanding – but the screenplay's editing of the book is genius. The scenes that did not survive into the film feel like DVD bonus features – Oo! A long deleted scene where Fezzik and Inigo have to make their way through the Zoo of Death! <br /><br />On the other hand, with a little more room for expansion and exploration than the movie affords, we get to know Buttercup's parents and Fezzik's parents, and also Domingo Montoya (a book line I plan to use: "'You're an enemy of art and I pity your ignorance,' Domingo said."); we see how Inigo got the scars and the vendetta. And the overall theme – life is not fair – can be taken more seriously than the book (or film) readily allows. <br /><br />"Life is pain," [Fezzik's] mother said [a line appropriated by the Dread Pirate Roberts in the film]. "Anybody that says different is selling something."<br /><br />Goldman says when someone explained this to him when he was young, he rejoiced – and I love that. There's a certain weight taken off your shoulders when suddenly it's made clear in no uncertain terms that: Life Is Not Fair. It's not supposed to be. It's not meant to be. You can stop being disappointed by the steady stream of crap life throws at you, and embrace reality: Life Is Fundamentally Unjust. Any fairness you happen to come across is either accidental or a state that was fought for and hard-won, and transient (or bought). The stories lie. A gentler way to put that is that the stories are not true, they're fairy tales, illustrations of what might be or might have been or never will be – but the core of it is that the stories lie. The wrong people get married. The wrong people get the wrong jobs. The wrong people die. <br /><br />Fortunately, in Florin there are Miracle Men who can help with that.<br /><br />However, Miracle Men – and others – make mistakes. That's life.<br /><br />Purity and loss of innocence are deeply underscored in the novel. Where the film was mostly a marvelously fun comic fantasy, the book digs a bit deeper, bites a little harder. Don't worry - I'm not about to commit an attempt at literary exploration of the themes; I'll leave that for the experts. Where I can speak from authority is on my own experience. The movie never made me well up when the boy demands to know <em>"Who gets Humperdinck?"</em> To which the response is, of course, "Nobody." It's like William Goldman's fictional(?) epiphany about life not, in fact, being fair. The incontrovertible fact that Prince Humperdinck richly deserves, in fact <em>needs</em> to be "got" does not, in fact, mean that he will be "got". Humiliated, beaten, stripped of the success of his plans and of some allies and of his prized Whites and so on, yes. Killed as he so richly deserves, which would be a satisfaction on a par to that felt when Count Rugen gets his? No. Sorry, kid. I really am sorry.<br /><br />Changing tacks: Fezzik in the book (not in the movie though) kept reminding me of someone, and it was after his reunion with Inigo that it struck me who that is. Fezzik is Pooh Bear. He is the self-proclaimed bear of very little brain, not learned or very quick thinking, but not ashamed of his lack, and possessed of an unexpected level of wisdom. (This would make Vizzini … Rabbit, perhaps? And I think Inigo must be Christopher Robin. Humperdinck might be a Heffalump.)<br /><br />It would be very easy to render this review as a sort of left-handed compliment, to hold it up against the unimaginably wonderful movie it spawned and let it fade a bit in the comparison. But I am not left-handed, and, in the end, this retains its adoring five-star rating. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7261428959729005550">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_42219053">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42219053" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1876075-cara" class="left imgcol" title="Cara"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1350665534p2/1876075.jpg" alt="Cara" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/42219053?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 12, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1876075-cara" class="user" title="Cara">Cara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/9525672-the-princess-bride" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=books-made-into-movies" class="actionLinkLite">books-made-into-movies</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=e-book" class="actionLinkLite">e-book</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=2015" class="actionLinkLite">2015</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=pop-sugar-2015-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">pop-sugar-2015-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer42219053">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11280289688676404422">I have been a member of this site since January 2009 (I know I am feeling pretty old these days!), and the very first book I put on my to-read list, you guessed it, was this one. So roughly five years later I have finally read it!<br /><br />So what is this book about? Well it depends who you ask. It’s about a tale of high adventure and true love. It’s about a girl named Buttercup and a farm boy named Westley. It’s about a Spanish fencer named Inigo Montoya and a giant named Fezzik. It’s about a blood thirs</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11280289688676404422">I have been a member of this site since January 2009 (I know I am feeling pretty old these days!), and the very first book I put on my to-read list, you guessed it, was this one. So roughly five years later I have finally read it!<br /><br />So what is this book about? Well it depends who you ask. It’s about a tale of high adventure and true love. It’s about a girl named Buttercup and a farm boy named Westley. It’s about a Spanish fencer named Inigo Montoya and a giant named Fezzik. It’s about a blood thirsty prince and a Count with six fingers. But it’s also about how life isn't fair and how the good guys sometimes can lose. I just touched and some of what the book is about. <br /><br />I believe to fully enjoy this book you have to be ok with the style. The story is told with two fake plot lines, so a story within a story. One is the story we all are expecting, about Buttercup’s and Westley’s adventure to be together and the other is Goldman talking about abridging this book from the Florin author named Morgenstern. I will admit the satire got to be a little too much for me, and I would get right down annoyed at times. The edition I read had introductions Goldman wrote for the 30th and 25th anniversary printings, which I skipped over because it’s more of the satire that I wasn't too keen on. That being said, I totally got caught up with the high jinks these characters got themselves into. This a tale you have to suspend belief for but part of the fun is how outlandish it is. It delivers on its promise of having sword fights, vengeance, miracles, monsters, pirates, and basically things you would expect on an epic adventure. One of the things Goldman does well is present the juxtaposition of life not being fair and yet the elusive chase for the happy ending we all strive for. There is something beautiful in the chase. Now enough of me babbling and go experience for yourself how this has become a modern classic. <br /><br /><strong>Side note:</strong> I couldn't leave you guys without mentioning the movie! <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=O3CIXEAjcc8">Here</a> is a link to the trailer if you are interested. It’s just one of the movies you <strong>
  <em>have</em>
</strong> to watch. <br /><br /><br />Read for <strong>POPSUGAR CHALLENGE 2015</strong>: A book at the bottom of your to-read list <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11280289688676404422">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_949255780">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/949255780" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/19468761-hershey" class="left imgcol" title="Hershey "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1411296149p2/19468761.jpg" alt="Hershey " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/949255780?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 29, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19468761-hershey" class="user" title="Hershey ">Hershey </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/6283231-the-princess-bride" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=2014-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2014-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer949255780">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10801213828131305386"><em>The Princess Bride</em> was a very <strong>fun</strong> and a <strong>delightful</strong> journey for me. I happen to love adventures and really, who doesn't? It's inconceivable to even think of a person who doesn't love adventures!<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401372316i/9793849._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Buttercup, our main character, had quite the adventure. Let me tell you, the best thing about this book is the characters. They're downright <strong>funny</strong>, <strong>adorable</strong>, <strong>brave</strong>, <strong>bold</strong> and most of all <strong>memorable.</strong> I loved every single one of them, especially Fezzik. I really found him very adorable!<br /><br />I laughed at several tim</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10801213828131305386"><em>The Princess Bride</em> was a very <strong>fun</strong> and a <strong>delightful</strong> journey for me. I happen to love adventures and really, who doesn't? It's inconceivable to even think of a person who doesn't love adventures!<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401372316i/9793849._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Buttercup, our main character, had quite the adventure. Let me tell you, the best thing about this book is the characters. They're downright <strong>funny</strong>, <strong>adorable</strong>, <strong>brave</strong>, <strong>bold</strong> and most of all <strong>memorable.</strong> I loved every single one of them, especially Fezzik. I really found him very adorable!<br /><br />I laughed at several times and I was completely shocked because I have never laughed so much while reading a book. Any book that makes you laugh is a good book!<br /><br />I don't really need to say much about the story. Most of you would have watched the movie or would have read the book a long time ago. I'm really late in reading all the good classics. If you're new to this book like I was, then go into it blind. You'll have an awesome and a memorable adventure, for sure.<br /><br />My only problem with the book was the parentheses or I would like to call them as 'The interruptions'. Sometimes, I enjoyed reading them. Sometimes, I skimmed them. Sometimes, I felt like throwing it against a wall. I didn't want to skip them because then I'd feel like I read an incomplete book (I'm weird, I know). So, if you have the same problems, just leave the book for some time. Go do something else and then come back to it. Don't force yourself to continue because it sure didn't work out for me. Read this book slowly and savor every bit of it.<br /><br /><u>
  <strong>The Princess Bride Equation</strong>
</u><br /><br /><strong>A Princess + Bad Guys + Good Guys + Action + Humor = Unforgettable Adventure</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401372316i/9793850._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />P.S: If you want to spook someone, ask them if they have six fingers and if they do tell them this:<br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401372875i/9793996._SY540_.jpg" /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_46683141">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46683141" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1884487-ash" class="left imgcol" title="Ash"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1291356919p2/1884487.jpg" alt="Ash" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/46683141?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 07, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1884487-ash" class="user" title="Ash">Ash</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780345418265" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer46683141">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12207628715328471902"> It’s incredibly hard for me to write a review for this book because I had such high expectations for it. At the same time though it was entertaining and had everything it promised: high action, revenge, miracles, and most importantly true love. I can't pinpoint exactly what it was that bothered me. What kept from loving it. <br /> At first I thought maybe it was the fact that the main characters didn't always seem to do the noble and honorable thing (sometimes I questioned if Westley and Buttercup re</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12207628715328471902"> It’s incredibly hard for me to write a review for this book because I had such high expectations for it. At the same time though it was entertaining and had everything it promised: high action, revenge, miracles, and most importantly true love. I can't pinpoint exactly what it was that bothered me. What kept from loving it. <br /> At first I thought maybe it was the fact that the main characters didn't always seem to do the noble and honorable thing (sometimes I questioned if Westley and Buttercup really loved each other or if they just loved the idea of each other), but then again I liked how it wasn't a typical fairy tale. I thought that parts where the author "interrupts" were funny, but sometimes they seemed long winded. At times I couldn't really get into the story because he would cut in. I wonder if because I watched the movie first it ruined the book for me. I loved the movie. It was funny and refreshingly different than all the other happily ever after movies that I watched when I was younger. My dad even liked the movie (he was the one who showed it to me and my brother and sisters) and let me tell you, my dad is the hard-core-burly-man type so trust me, it was a good movie if he liked it. <br /><br />I really wanted to like this book so much more and it seems like there must be something wrong with me for not absolutely loving it. Maybe it was the fact that the author really lays it on thick, saying that these events actually happened. Telling you these characters actually existed as do the places. He talks about how the "original" story was written by some guy named Morgenstern, who by the way doesn't exist. I’m fairly sure that most of the stuff he wrote about himself wasn't true either, although I do know some of it is. I knew that none of that stuff was true from the beginning though. Before I even started reading it, so I can't say that's really the reason. One thing that really bothered me at times was how much he tried to fake you out. I guess I wasn't supposed to know when he was faking you out, but since I watched the movie I knew what to expect. <br /><br />I can't say that I loved this book, but I can see why people would love it so much. You have to read the book yourself because it's one of those stories that you have to make your own opinion about. I really enjoyed the last chapter "The Remora". Also the "first chapter" of the "Sequel: Buttercup's Baby", I use quotations because, as per usual, it's not really true. The chapter was interesting, although I was kinda peeved that he ruined the happily ever after that I usually like. I still liked it though. I liked the book too, but didn't absolutely love it. There were really touching parts as well as funny ones. My favorite character was probably Inigo and I wish I could see how his story ends. Read it and see what's your opinion.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12207628715328471902">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_598228049">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/598228049" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6610433-midnightfaerie" class="left imgcol" title="midnightfaerie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1318372863p2/6610433.jpg" alt="midnightfaerie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/598228049?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 21, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6610433-midnightfaerie" class="user" title="midnightfaerie">midnightfaerie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride" title="Paperback 9780345418265" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6610433-midnightfaerie?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer598228049">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4927896547932193969">Choppy, but I suspect it was meant as such, considering it was written as mostly a screenplay and edited by a writer (If you can call him that) who had no concern whatsoever in preserving the sanctity of the original author's intent. A cut here, a slash there, S. Morgenstern's Classic Tale is ripped to pieces under William Goldman's butchering knife. He justifies it by the fact that he leaves a few chapters untouched, yet can't help but interject his unwanted thoughts upon his poor unsuspecting</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4927896547932193969">Choppy, but I suspect it was meant as such, considering it was written as mostly a screenplay and edited by a writer (If you can call him that) who had no concern whatsoever in preserving the sanctity of the original author's intent. A cut here, a slash there, S. Morgenstern's Classic Tale is ripped to pieces under William Goldman's butchering knife. He justifies it by the fact that he leaves a few chapters untouched, yet can't help but interject his unwanted thoughts upon his poor unsuspecting readers. <br /><br />Okay, perhaps I was a bit rough on Goldman, but it was choppy. And Morgenstern's brilliance makes him a hero. Which is easy to do when one doesn't exist. And maybe it was just because I didn't like Goldman much. The way he described his wife and his fat child, got under my skin. He seemed a bit self-absorbed to me, and the fact that he resolved the issue later on with his child really made no difference to me. <br /><br />That being said, the actual story was engaging and rather sort of brilliant, but I still found it a little too abrupt for real enjoyment. Every time I started to get into the story, I was interrupted. It wasn't as silly as the movie I had seen years ago, and even though it was pretty much the same story, reading it, it didn't seem as silly. I loved the politeness of the dialogue, the satire between characters, and unlike Goldman, the continual explanations of historical events in parenthesis throughout the story. (Knowing it was written way before parenthesis actually existed.) I was tickled by faulty logic and the made-up terrible beasts, R.O.U.S.'s. The characters were engaging and fun if not idiotic, and the book seemed to diminish Buttercup's intelligence to less than nothing. <br /><br />I love lighthearted stories but there was no depth to anything and so it was hard to get into any aspect of the story. For example how could I believe that their kiss was even better than the top five kisses ever to have been, if I can't even understand their love for each other? They spent time together for years, but what was it that drew them together? Shared interests? Invigorating conversation? Hardly possible (or perhaps inconceivable) if all he ever said was "As you wish." It made me feel as if their attraction was based solely on looks and I had a hard time buying into that kind of love. And then there was one of their first conversations where she made a comment and he said something like "Well, be both know you're not that bright." And she agreed! (I love you til the ends of the earth and I'm glad you know there won't be any stimulating conversation between us because I'm dumber than a box of rocks.) <br /><br />It's not that I don't appreciate silly, there are some stories that go beyond silly that I'm enraptured with. (The best example off the top of my head I can think of it the movie Crybaby with Johnny Depp) I just had a longing for more information from this book. When I finished reading it, I felt a strong desire to read the original book, to see if Goldman was lying about the tedious and unneeded chapters. Which is when I realized it didn't exist, and that's when the realization of Goldman's brilliance set in. It really was a rather clever ruse masquerading as a literary device. <br /><br />Overall, it was a fun read for me. Nothing really stood out as exceptional except maybe the style of writing, the politeness in combat, the Aha! moments, none of which had anything to do with Goldman's writing. It was all Morgenstern's. A recent rewatch of the movie that I had pretty much forgotten most of, considering I hadn't seen it for over ten years, yielded nothing extraordinary for me, except an extra added greatness of Fezznik's character, and once again, a silliness that was even more evident in the movie than the book. I understand the leaning toward cultdom for this story, and I recognize the originality that makes it great, but it just isn't my cup of proverbial tea. <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://classicsdefined.com/princessbride.html"> ClassicsDefined.com</a><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4927896547932193969">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12411569057317334978">There was no Morgenstern. Author William Goldman made up the character as a bit of whimsy, just as he refers to Florin and Guilder as real countries i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12411569057317334978">There was no Morgenstern. Author William Goldman made up the character as a bit of whimsy, just as he refers to Florin and Guilder as real countries in Europe ( in the 30th anniversary of The Princess Bride, Goldman even "visits" the Morgenstern museum in "Florin" with his grandson). Goldman is the Academy award winning screenwriter of "Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid', "Marathon Man", "All the President's Men" and "The Ghost and the Darkness." <br /><br />Goldman goes into his creation of the novel in his book ""Which Lie Did I Tell: More Adventures in the Screen Trade. (2000)<br /><br />The Princess Bride was written as a tongue in cheek satire of the fantasy adventure genre. You just have to get used to Goldman's sense of humor.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/664756441?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 08, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/22110057-debbie-zapata" class="user" title="Debbie Zapata">Debbie Zapata</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/828035.The_Princess_Bride" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345315328" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/22110057-debbie-zapata?shelf=eyesome" class="actionLinkLite">eyesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer664756441">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18279461722588766765">I am in a swashbuckling mood these days and it is all Westley's fault. After recently reading <a title="As You Wish Inconceivable Tales from the Making of The Princess Bride by Cary Elwes" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21412202.As_You_Wish_Inconceivable_Tales_from_the_Making_of_The_Princess_Bride">As You Wish: Inconceivable Tales from the Making of The Princess Bride</a> , written by Cary Elwes, I HAD to re-read The Princess Bride for the umpty-eleventh time. And I loved it as usual.<br /><br />But I can clearly not let this review go by without saying that while The Princess Bride is supposed to be an abridgment of the S. Morgenstern classic of the same name, the screenplay for the movie is an abridgment of <em>thi</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18279461722588766765">I am in a swashbuckling mood these days and it is all Westley's fault. After recently reading <a title="As You Wish Inconceivable Tales from the Making of The Princess Bride by Cary Elwes" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21412202.As_You_Wish_Inconceivable_Tales_from_the_Making_of_The_Princess_Bride">As You Wish: Inconceivable Tales from the Making of The Princess Bride</a> , written by Cary Elwes, I HAD to re-read The Princess Bride for the umpty-eleventh time. And I loved it as usual.<br /><br />But I can clearly not let this review go by without saying that while The Princess Bride is supposed to be an abridgment of the S. Morgenstern classic of the same name, the screenplay for the movie is an abridgment of <em>this</em> book. In other words, the movie has all the best parts of this book, just as this book has all the best parts of Morgenstern's book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[(And we all know, I hope, that there really was no 'Morgenstern's book'. The whole thing came from William Goldman's clever imagination.) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> My point is that anyone who has only seen the movie might not appreciate the book quite as much as those who read before heading to Netflix. <br /><br />Goldman breaks into the story every so often to explain that when he was a child he had never heard this or that part of the story because his father skipped it. Chapter Four (it is one page long) is a perfect example of this little trick. But for me these interruptions have never been annoying, they just add to the charm of the book. However, when I was just about to have fun storming the castle, my husband got home and I had to put the book down until after lunch. I finished storming then, but I'm going to go back now and <br />re-read that section for the umpty-twelfth time just to be able to do it in one take. <!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18279461722588766765">...more</a>

      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y85S/xQpJqfnxbE9FBY0xmnyGvudkEurxhmCzGYMc5QGGm0s5vsyXWsdxYZqd9J0IAXZ4tRNDAGsEIdeqpmF0Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rtxC4HPeufhArx3/z/RB8bjssv/i8lC+JPTg48/sB8jLCH0zgQytAsx3aUSxladD8Rtx5qsvFxRO/eVxA3nxjQ==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12521.William_Goldman">About William Goldman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/12521.William_Goldman"><img alt="12521" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1198704782p2/12521.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer8987480453411982397">Goldman grew up in a Jewish family in Highland Park, Illinois, a Chicago suburb, and obtained a BA degree at Oberlin College in 1952 and an MA degree at Columbia University in 1956.His brother was the late <a title="James Goldman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12524.James_Goldman">James Goldman</a>, author and playwright.<br /><br />William Goldman had published five novels and had three plays produced on Broadway before he began to write screenplays. Several of his novels he later used</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8987480453411982397">Goldman grew up in a Jewish family in Highland Park, Illinois, a Chicago suburb, and obtained a BA degree at Oberlin College in 1952 and an MA degree at Columbia University in 1956.His brother was the late <a title="James Goldman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12524.James_Goldman">James Goldman</a>, author and playwright.<br /><br />William Goldman had published five novels and had three plays produced on Broadway before he began to write screenplays. Several of his novels he later used as the foundation for his screenplays. In the 1980s he wrote a series of memoirs looking at his professional life on Broadway and in Hollywood (in one of these he famously remarked that "Nobody knows anything"). He then returned to writing novels. He then adapted his novel <a title="The Princess Bride  by William Goldman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride_">The Princess Bride</a> to the <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0093779/">screen</a>, which marked his re-entry into screenwriting. <br />Goldman has won two Academy Awards: an Academy Award for Writing Original Screenplay for <em>Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid</em>, and an Academy Award for Writing Adapted Screenplay for <em>All the President's Men</em>. He has also won two Edgar Awards, from the Mystery Writers of America, for Best Motion Picture Screenplay: for <em>Harper </em>in 1967, and for <em>Magic</em> (adapted from his own 1976 novel) in 1979.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8987480453411982397">...more</a>

    </div>
